Thanks!  This looks like it covers the most important part of what I'm looking for.&#010;&#010;&#010;-----Original Message-----&#010;From: Mark Derricutt [mailto:mark@talios.com] &#010;Sent: Tuesday, September 30, 2014 5:04 PM&#010;To: Maven Users List&#010;Subject: Re: Maven, Dependencies and Vulnerabilities&#010;&#010;On 1 Oct 2014, at 7:44, David Dillard wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've been working on an internal presentation on how letting Maven's &#010;&gt; dependency mediation feature select versions of transitive &#010;&gt; dependencies can introduce vulnerabilities into a product and how to &#010;&gt; deal with that problem.  Unfortunately, it's a very manual process and &#010;&gt; I was thinking that perhaps changes could be made to Maven that would &#010;&gt; provide better automation.  To that end I'm wondering if the team has &#010;&gt; ever considered adding a section to the POM that would list &#010;&gt; significant changes in that release.  This would include a list of &#010;&gt; vulnerabilities fixed (e.g. CVE-XXXX-YYYY) or serious bugs fixed.&#010;&gt; Each one could include a known set of versions affected (ala how CVEs &#010;&gt; work today) thus allowing tooling to say: the version of artifact XYZ &#010;&gt; you're using has a known vulnerability, would you like to upgrade to &#010;&gt; this new version with that vuln fixed?&#010;&#010;There already exists a plugin covering a lot of this, using the CVE&#010;databases:&#010;&#010;   https://github.com/jeremylong/DependencyCheck&#010;&#010;This comes with a CLI, Jenkins, Maven, and Ant tasks for checking your dependencies/jars against&#010;CVE vulnerabilities.&#010;&#010;Does this cover all the things you're working on?  Maybe join forces?&#010;&#010;&#010;Mark&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
I'm familiar with Black Duck and an older version of Palamida.  The problem with them is that&#010;you see the vulnerabilities later in the dev cycle (usually).  If done with Maven it could&#010;be a part of the build and thus found earlier.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;I like the idea of including the CPE in the POM and that would make finding CVEs easy enough.&#010; Only issue there is, as you noted, that projects would have to submit to get their CPE before&#010;they have any vulnerabilities.  Has anyone suggested this before?&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;-----Original Message-----&#013;&#010;From: Jeremy Long [mailto:jeremy.long@gmail.com] &#013;&#010;Sent: Tuesday, September 30, 2014 3:53 PM&#013;&#010;To: Maven Users List&#013;&#010;Subject: Re: Maven, Dependencies and Vulnerabilities&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;There are commercial solutions (sonatype, contrast, blackduck, palamida,&#013;&#010;etc.) and FOSS solutions (dependency-check, victims, retire.js, etc.) to identify and report&#010;on known vulnerabilities. I would recommend looking at these solutions (note, I am the main&#010;contributed to dependency-check).&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;A better solution for the POM modification would be to add a CPE identifier. This would also&#010;be a great entry for a jar file's manifest. CPE identifiers can be requested even if there&#010;are no known CVEs, but the CPE can be used to lookup the related CVEs.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;-jeremy&#013;&#010;@ctxt&#013;&#010;On Sep 30, 2014 2:45 PM, "David Dillard" &lt;ddillard@symantec.com&gt; wrote:&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; I've been working on an internal presentation on how letting Maven's &#013;&#010;&gt; dependency mediation feature select versions of transitive &#013;&#010;&gt; dependencies can introduce vulnerabilities into a product and how to &#013;&#010;&gt; deal with that problem.  Unfortunately, it's a very manual process and &#013;&#010;&gt; I was thinking that perhaps changes could be made to Maven that would &#013;&#010;&gt; provide better automation.  To that end I'm wondering if the team has &#013;&#010;&gt; ever considered adding a section to the POM that would list &#013;&#010;&gt; significant changes in that release.  This would include a list of vulnerabilities fixed&#010;(e.g.&#013;&#010;&gt; CVE-XXXX-YYYY) or serious bugs fixed.  Each one could include a known &#013;&#010;&gt; set of versions affected (ala how CVEs work today) thus allowing &#013;&#010;&gt; tooling to&#013;&#010;&gt; say: the version of artifact XYZ you're using has a known &#013;&#010;&gt; vulnerability, would you like to upgrade to this new version with that vuln fixed?&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; On a related note, has a different dependency mediation system ever &#013;&#010;&gt; been considered (as an option), e.g. latest version or latest version &#013;&#010;&gt; on a branch?&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; David&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;

contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;instead of requiring everybody to come up with a CPE and add it to the POM,&#010;I would prefer if Maven Central publishes an approved (and registered)&#010;naming scheme to form CPEs which point to well known maven artifacts.&#010;&#010;cpe:/a:org.maven.central:groupid,artifactid[,classifier]:version&#010;(or similiar, maybe ask the CPE team about it. alternative would be to have&#010;a common maven-style repo vendor and include the repoid in the "product")&#010;&#010;This would allow incidents and CVEs to unambigously refer to libraries and&#010;other artifacts.&#010;&#010;The Java eco system is really missing good reports based on open source&#010;components. If you are lucky you find an alert based on a product and can&#010;guess what underlying open source component was vulnerable. This makes (as&#010;you know) the life of a scanner pretty hard.&#010;&#010;Gruss&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-09-30 21:53 GMT+02:00 Jeremy Long &lt;jeremy.long@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; There are commercial solutions (sonatype, contrast, blackduck, palamida,&#010;&gt; etc.) and FOSS solutions (dependency-check, victims, retire.js, etc.) to&#010;&gt; identify and report on known vulnerabilities. I would recommend looking at&#010;&gt; these solutions (note, I am the main contributed to dependency-check).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A better solution for the POM modification would be to add a CPE&#010;&gt; identifier. This would also be a great entry for a jar file's manifest. CPE&#010;&gt; identifiers can be requested even if there are no known CVEs, but the CPE&#010;&gt; can be used to lookup the related CVEs.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -jeremy&#010;&gt; @ctxt&#010;&gt; On Sep 30, 2014 2:45 PM, "David Dillard" &lt;ddillard@symantec.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I've been working on an internal presentation on how letting Maven's&#010;&gt; &gt; dependency mediation feature select versions of transitive dependencies&#010;&gt; can&#010;&gt; &gt; introduce vulnerabilities into a product and how to deal with that&#010;&gt; &gt; problem.  Unfortunately, it's a very manual process and I was thinking&#010;&gt; that&#010;&gt; &gt; perhaps changes could be made to Maven that would provide better&#010;&gt; &gt; automation.  To that end I'm wondering if the team has ever considered&#010;&gt; &gt; adding a section to the POM that would list significant changes in that&#010;&gt; &gt; release.  This would include a list of vulnerabilities fixed (e.g.&#010;&gt; &gt; CVE-XXXX-YYYY) or serious bugs fixed.  Each one could include a known set&#010;&gt; &gt; of versions affected (ala how CVEs work today) thus allowing tooling to&#010;&gt; &gt; say: the version of artifact XYZ you're using has a known vulnerability,&#010;&gt; &gt; would you like to upgrade to this new version with that vuln fixed?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On a related note, has a different dependency mediation system ever been&#010;&gt; &gt; considered (as an option), e.g. latest version or latest version on a&#010;&gt; &gt; branch?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; David&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
A couple of potential problems with that:&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;1. If an existing CPE doesn't follow whatever convention is decided upon or worse the convention&#010;creates a CPE for one project that's already in use by a different project (admittedly that's&#010;unlikely)&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;2. When names change (e.g. the artifact ID) that would likely change the CPE, but you probably&#010;don't want the CPE to change otherwise you'll have two (or more CPEs) referring to the same&#010;project.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;-----Original Message-----&#013;&#010;From: Bernd [mailto:ecki@zusammenkunft.net] &#013;&#010;Sent: Monday, October 13, 2014 12:48 PM&#013;&#010;To: Maven Users List&#013;&#010;Subject: Re: Maven, Dependencies and Vulnerabilities&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;Hello,&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;instead of requiring everybody to come up with a CPE and add it to the POM, I would prefer&#010;if Maven Central publishes an approved (and registered) naming scheme to form CPEs which point&#010;to well known maven artifacts.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;cpe:/a:org.maven.central:groupid,artifactid[,classifier]:version&#013;&#010;(or similiar, maybe ask the CPE team about it. alternative would be to have a common maven-style&#010;repo vendor and include the repoid in the "product")&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;This would allow incidents and CVEs to unambigously refer to libraries and other artifacts.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;The Java eco system is really missing good reports based on open source components. If you&#010;are lucky you find an alert based on a product and can guess what underlying open source component&#010;was vulnerable. This makes (as you know) the life of a scanner pretty hard.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;Gruss&#013;&#010;Bernd&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;2014-09-30 21:53 GMT+02:00 Jeremy Long &lt;jeremy.long@gmail.com&gt;:&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&gt; There are commercial solutions (sonatype, contrast, blackduck, &#013;&#010;&gt; palamida,&#013;&#010;&gt; etc.) and FOSS solutions (dependency-check, victims, retire.js, etc.) &#013;&#010;&gt; to identify and report on known vulnerabilities. I would recommend &#013;&#010;&gt; looking at these solutions (note, I am the main contributed to dependency-check).&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; A better solution for the POM modification would be to add a CPE &#013;&#010;&gt; identifier. This would also be a great entry for a jar file's &#013;&#010;&gt; manifest. CPE identifiers can be requested even if there are no known &#013;&#010;&gt; CVEs, but the CPE can be used to lookup the related CVEs.&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; -jeremy&#013;&#010;&gt; @ctxt&#013;&#010;&gt; On Sep 30, 2014 2:45 PM, "David Dillard" &lt;ddillard@symantec.com&gt; wrote:&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi,&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; I've been working on an internal presentation on how letting Maven's &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; dependency mediation feature select versions of transitive &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; dependencies&#013;&#010;&gt; can&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; introduce vulnerabilities into a product and how to deal with that &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; problem.  Unfortunately, it's a very manual process and I was &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; thinking&#013;&#010;&gt; that&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; perhaps changes could be made to Maven that would provide better &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; automation.  To that end I'm wondering if the team has ever &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; considered adding a section to the POM that would list significant &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; changes in that release.  This would include a list of vulnerabilities fixed (e.g.&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; CVE-XXXX-YYYY) or serious bugs fixed.  Each one could include a &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; known set of versions affected (ala how CVEs work today) thus &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; allowing tooling to&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; say: the version of artifact XYZ you're using has a known &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; vulnerability, would you like to upgrade to this new version with that vuln fixed?&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; On a related note, has a different dependency mediation system ever &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; been considered (as an option), e.g. latest version or latest &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; version on a branch?&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; Thanks,&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; David&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#013;&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#013;&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#013;&#010;

Announcing the NAR plugin for Maven 3.2.0  
Date  :-
Thu, 02 Oct 2014 17:12:15 GMT  
contents:- 
---------- Forwarded message ----------&#010;From: Johannes Schindelin &lt;Johannes.Schindelin@gmx.de&gt;&#010;Date: Thu, Oct 2, 2014 at 12:05 PM&#010;Subject: [maven-nar] Announcing the NAR plugin for Maven 3.2.0&#010;To: maven-nar@googlegroups.com&#010;&#010;&#010;Dear Maven users,&#010;&#010;it is a great honor to announce a new version of the NAR plugin for Maven,&#010;designed to support cross-platform development using JNI libraries.&#010;&#010;As always, this release would not be possible without a thriving developer&#010;community.  Here is the shortlog:&#010;&#010;    26  Johannes Schindelin&#010;    21  Fredrik Orderud&#010;    14  Curtis Rueden&#010;     8  HongKee Moon&#010;     5  Benson Margulies&#010;     2  Sevag Doniguian&#010;     1  Wouter Pasman&#010;     1  Ivan Drobyshevskyi&#010;     1  Mark Hiner&#010;     1  Philippe Marschall&#010;     1  Tomasz Krakowiak&#010;     1  Trevor Robinson&#010;&#010;These are the changes since version 3.1.0 (the parenthesized numbers refer&#010;to pull requests of https://github.com/maven-nar/nar-maven-plugin).&#010;&#010;Bug fixes:&#010;&#010;- The description of the examples now mentions explicitly that they are&#010;  integration tests (#109)&#010;&#010;- We use a newer maven-site-plugin version to fix a breakage (#113)&#010;&#010;- The documentation now talks about narSystemPackage where it talked&#010;  about the non-existent packageName before (#110)&#010;&#010;- The licensing was cleaned up (#120)&#010;&#010;- We now use the more appropriate msvc label for Microsoft Visual C/C++&#010;  instead of devstudio (#123)&#010;&#010;- The history.xml file included into the .nar artifacts is now actually&#010;  properly named, and as a consequence properly populated, too (#114)&#010;&#010;- The documentation no longer references the incorrect &lt;arch&gt; tag but&#010;  correctly calls it &lt;architecture&gt; (#132)&#010;&#010;- The web site no longer suggests that the NAR plugin is an official&#010;  Apache project (this was the original intention, but it never became&#010;  reality) (#133)&#010;&#010;- On Windows, inconsistent usage of the environment variable Path was&#010;  fixed (#134)&#010;&#010;- Fixed dead links in the documentation (#136)&#010;&#010;- Grammar sweep of the documentation (#137)&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010;- A new integration test demonstrates how to use a JNI .nar from a .jar&#010;  file (#112)&#010;&#010;- The AOL properties are now documented (#115)&#010;&#010;- It is now possible to filter which headers are included in the&#010;  artifacts (#124)&#010;&#010;- We joined the 21st century by using generics now (#127)&#010;&#010;- It is now possible to develop NAR projects in Eclipse even if they use&#010;  the NarSystem class (#130)&#010;&#010;- We now use the Maven 3.0.4 platform (#118)&#010;&#010;- Support was added for the VisualAge compiler on AIX (#131)&#010;&#010;- The web site now uses the very pretty fluido skin and sports the NAR&#010;  logo prominently (#133)&#010;&#010;The new look of the web site can be adored here:&#010;https://maven-nar.github.io/&#010;&#010;On behalf of all the developers making the NAR plugin awesome,&#010;Johannes&#010;&#010;--&#010;You received this message because you are subscribed to the Google Groups&#010;"NAR Maven plugin" group.&#010;To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it, send an&#010;email to maven-nar+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com.&#010;For more options, visit https://groups.google.com/d/optout.&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Re: WAR contains SNAPSHOT JARs with timestamps  
Date  :-
Sun, 05 Oct 2014 02:41:46 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;I would argue this is a feature not a bug. (And this is also the&#010;version name which IS stored in the repo). &#010;&#010;Anyway, the WAR plugin uses the archiver shared component and that&#010;allows to specify a custom classpath pattern, which should work to&#010;remove the version component:&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-archiver/examples/classpath.html#aContents&#010;&#010;If you want to only keep the -SNAPSHOT, then you can use&#010;useUniqueVersions=false&#010;&#010;Gruss&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;&#010; Am Fri, 3 Oct 2014 07:46:35 -0700 (PDT)&#010;schrieb captainslow &lt;srinivas.nagesh@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have this project setup which uses Webstart and I need to bundle&#010;&gt; the WAR with SNAPSHOT JARs. When the JARs are bundled into the WAR,&#010;&gt; they are appended with a timestamp instead of the actual name. &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Expected - ABC-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &#010;&gt; Actual - ABC-1.0-20141002.211448-2.jar&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The JAR in the remote repository (Artifactory) and local M2 repo is&#010;&gt; showing up as ABC-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Env:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; OS: Unix&#010;&gt; Maven: 3.2.1&#010;&gt; JDK: 1.7&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Any thoughts on what needs to be done to get it to bundle with just&#010;&gt; the name?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/WAR-contains-SNAPSHOT-JARs-with-timestamps-tp5807695.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Running integration tests  
Date  :-
Mon, 06 Oct 2014 09:31:32 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi All,&#010;&#010;A couple of questions about integration tests..&#010;&#010;&#010;1) Default vs non-default plugins&#010;I needed to include the maven-failsafe-plugin plugin to introduce&#010;integration tests into my project, but I didn't need to introduce the&#010;maven-surefire-plugin to my pom.xml for unit tests. Fair enough, but&#010;how do I know which plugins are included by default?&#010;&#010;2) Just run integration tests?&#010;I can see that unit tests are all classes with names like *Test.java&#010;and integration tests are all classes with names like IT.java. But mvn&#010;verify and mvn test seem to run all tests (unit and integrations). Is&#010;there a way to run just one or the other?&#010;&#010;3) Run integration tests after compile?&#010;The real reason for question 2 is that I wish to run integration tests&#010;only after I have deployed the new application to ensure the&#010;integration tests run on the server with the new content. Is there a&#010;way to do this?&#010;&#010;Thanks for any assistance!&#010;&#010;Rob&#010;:)&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Running integration tests  
Date  :-
Mon, 06 Oct 2014 10:16:27 GMT

On 6 October 2014 10:31, Robert Mark Bram &lt;robertmarkbram@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A couple of questions about integration tests..&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1) Default vs non-default plugins&#010;&gt; I needed to include the maven-failsafe-plugin plugin to introduce&#010;&gt; integration tests into my project, but I didn't need to introduce the&#010;&gt; maven-surefire-plugin to my pom.xml for unit tests. Fair enough, but&#010;&gt; how do I know which plugins are included by default?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&gt; suddenly a White Rabbit with pink eyes ran close by Alice&#010;&#010;In your pom.xml there is a xml node /project/packaging that specifies the&#010;lifecycle for your project.&#010;&#010;You may not have set the value to anything, as the default if unspecified&#010;is: jar&#010;&#010;&gt; There was nothing so very remarkable in that; nor did Alice think it so&#010;very much out of the way to hear the Rabbit say to itself "Oh dear! Oh&#010;dear! I shall be too late!"&#010;&#010;Maven consults all the registered extensions and the core functionality to&#010;see what lifecycles are registered for the packaging of the module it is&#010;building.&#010;&#010;In general it will end up here:&#010;https://github.com/apache/maven/blob/276c7636d342f6d01353ae862b56fa89614b17a9/maven-core/src/main/resources/META-INF/plexus/components.xml#L33&#010;&#010;&gt; but, when the Rabbit actually took a watch out of its waistcoat-pocket,&#010;and looked at it, and then hurried on, Alice started to her feet, for it&#010;flashed across her mind that she had never before seen a rabbit with either&#010;a waistcoat-pocket, or a watch to take out of it, and burning with&#010;curiosity, she ran across the field after it, and was just in time to see&#010;it pop down a large rabbit-hole under the hedge.&#010;&#010;Once Maven has determined the lifecycle(s) that apply to your module, it&#010;then looks up the phases and goals that you specified when invoking Maven.&#010;&#010;&gt;From this list of phases and goals it starts to construct the build plan...&#010;&#010;Conceptually, at the start the build plan is just the list of phases to&#010;execute.&#010;&#010;So for example you type: `mvn clean install clean deploy site-deploy`&#010;&#010;Then Maven says, ok clean comes from the `clean` lifecycle, and it is the&#010;second phase... so we will start off with: pre-clean, clean&#010;&#010;Next we need install, so that's from the default lifecycle and we will add&#010;in the phases: validate, initialize, generate-sources, process-sources,&#010;generate-resources, process-resources, compile, process-classes,&#010;generate-test-sources, process-test-sources, generate-test-resources,&#010;process-test-resources, test-compile, process-test-classes, test,&#010;prepare-package, package, pre-integration-test, integration-test,&#010;post-integration-test, verify, install&#010;&#010;Then we need another clean... at this point our list will be looking like:&#010;pre-clean, clean, validate, initialize, generate-sources, process-sources,&#010;generate-resources, process-resources, compile, process-classes,&#010;generate-test-sources, process-test-sources, generate-test-resources,&#010;process-test-resources, test-compile, process-test-classes, test,&#010;prepare-package, package, pre-integration-test, integration-test,&#010;post-integration-test, verify, install, pre-clean, clean&#010;&#010;Then we need to go all the way up to deploy... so we'll have: pre-clean,&#010;clean, validate, initialize, generate-sources, process-sources,&#010;generate-resources, process-resources, compile, process-classes,&#010;generate-test-sources, process-test-sources, generate-test-resources,&#010;process-test-resources, test-compile, process-test-classes, test,&#010;prepare-package, package, pre-integration-test, integration-test,&#010;post-integration-test, verify, install, pre-clean, clean, validate,&#010;initialize, generate-sources, process-sources, generate-resources,&#010;process-resources, compile, process-classes, generate-test-sources,&#010;process-test-sources, generate-test-resources, process-test-resources,&#010;test-compile, process-test-classes, test, prepare-package, package,&#010;pre-integration-test, integration-test, post-integration-test, verify,&#010;install, deploy&#010;&#010;And finally we need to run up the site lifecycle as far as site-deploy...&#010;so now the complete list of phases to execute in order are: pre-clean,&#010;clean, validate, initialize, generate-sources, process-sources,&#010;generate-resources, process-resources, compile, process-classes,&#010;generate-test-sources, process-test-sources, generate-test-resources,&#010;process-test-resources, test-compile, process-test-classes, test,&#010;prepare-package, package, pre-integration-test, integration-test,&#010;post-integration-test, verify, install, pre-clean, clean, validate,&#010;initialize, generate-sources, process-sources, generate-resources,&#010;process-resources, compile, process-classes, generate-test-sources,&#010;process-test-sources, generate-test-resources, process-test-resources,&#010;test-compile, process-test-classes, test, prepare-package, package,&#010;pre-integration-test, integration-test, post-integration-test, verify,&#010;install, deploy, pre-site, site, post-site, site-deploy&#010;&#010;&gt; In another moment down went Alice after it, never once considering how in&#010;the world she was to get out again.&#010;&#010;Now Maven needs to decide exactly what it should do for each of those&#010;phases.&#010;&#010;So it starts by considering the default bindings: These again are&#010;determined by the packaging. In the case of the jar packaging from core&#010;that is defined here:&#010;https://github.com/apache/maven/blob/276c7636d342f6d01353ae862b56fa89614b17a9/maven-core/src/main/resources/META-INF/plexus/default-bindings.xml&#010;&#010;So everywhere that Maven sees the `test` phase it will add a binding of&#010;surefire:&#010;https://github.com/apache/maven/blob/276c7636d342f6d01353ae862b56fa89614b17a9/maven-core/src/main/resources/META-INF/plexus/default-bindings.xml#L82&#010;the binding defined the default plugin version but if you specify a&#010;different plugin version in your pom then the default is overridden.&#010;&#010;Next Maven looks at the effective pom for your project to see if there are&#010;any executions that are bound to phases.&#010;&#010;At the end of this process, maven now has a list of ordered plugin goal&#010;executions... and away it goes&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) Just run integration tests?&#010;&gt; I can see that unit tests are all classes with names like *Test.java&#010;&gt; and integration tests are all classes with names like IT.java. But mvn&#010;&gt; verify and mvn test seem to run all tests (unit and integrations). Is&#010;&gt; there a way to run just one or the other?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;tweaking of&#010;http://maven.apache.org/surefire/maven-surefire-plugin/test-mojo.html#skipTests&#010;should get you there!&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3) Run integration tests after compile?&#010;&gt; The real reason for question 2 is that I wish to run integration tests&#010;&gt; only after I have deployed the new application to ensure the&#010;&gt; integration tests run on the server with the new content. Is there a&#010;&gt; way to do this?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;Sounds like you should consult my answer to a related question:&#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/16935290/maven-deploy-webapp-to-tomcat-before-junit-test/16936585#16936585&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks for any assistance!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Rob&#010;&gt; :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Thank you Stephen - this was very useful and came just when I am ready&#010;to start piecing together this level of detail.&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; 1) Default vs non-default plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; suddenly a White Rabbit with pink eyes ran close by Alice&#010;&#010;So, what I understood from this trip down the rabbit-hole.&#010;- Maven defines various lifecycles.&#010;- Each lifecycle defines a list of phases.&#010;- Each phase will execute a list of goals (defined in plugins).&#010;- What specific goals get executed in each phase depends on the&#010;packaging defined for the pom.xml. Generally package defines what sort&#010;of artifact you are dealing with: jar, war, ear etc.&#010;- I am using ear packaging, so it binds the surefire:test goal to the&#010;test phase, but binds nothing to integration-test - which is why I&#010;need to add the failsafe plugin to my pom.xml. I didn't need to define&#010;a phase for it, because failsafe's default phase is integration-test.&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; 2) Just run integration tests?&#010;&gt; &gt; I can see that unit tests are all classes with names like *Test.java&#010;&gt; &gt; and integration tests are all classes with names like IT.java. But mvn&#010;&gt; &gt; verify and mvn test seem to run all tests (unit and integrations). Is&#010;&gt; &gt; there a way to run just one or the other?&#010;&#010;So, going from the previous trip down the rabbit hole, I understand&#010;that when I run "mvn verify" I was seeing unit tests and integration&#010;tests being run because in order to get to the verify phase (where my&#010;integration tests should run from), it was running every phase before&#010;that - including the test phase (where unit tests are run).&#010;&#010;&gt; tweaking of&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/surefire/maven-surefire-plugin/test-mojo.html#skipTests&#010;&gt; should get you there!&#010;&#010;When I was running "mvn test", I was also seeing integration tests&#010;being run because I had named my integration test classes&#010;TestBlahBlahIt.java so they were being picked up by both the test and&#010;integration-test phases.&#010;&#010;So, I should more strictly follow the convention of&#010;- unit tests being Test*.java - and NOT including IT at the end.&#010;- integration tests being *.IT.java - and NOT starting with Test.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; 3) Run integration tests after compile?&#010;&gt; &gt; The real reason for question 2 is that I wish to run integration tests&#010;&gt; &gt; only after I have deployed the new application to ensure the&#010;&gt; &gt; integration tests run on the server with the new content. Is there a&#010;&gt; &gt; way to do this?&#010;&#010;&gt; Sounds like you should consult my answer to a related question:&#010;&gt; http://stackoverflow.com/questions/16935290/maven-deploy-webapp-to-tomcat-before-junit-test/16936585#16936585&#010;&#010;OK, this was very helpful too. In this case, I am working with a&#010;multi-module project and I decided it was best to add our selenium&#010;tests in a new project to keep them away from other project code. We&#010;have 13 pom.xml files, not counting the one I am adding. So this is my&#010;next challenge, to ensure I get this project executing after the&#010;others have done their job and deployed to the app server.&#010;&#010;Why, sometimes I've believed as many as five impossible things before&#010;after-noon tea. Time for one more before I knock off at 5pm.&#010;&#010;Rob&#010;:)&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarba...@gmx.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Running integration tests  
Date  :-
Wed, 08 Oct 2014 09:55:57 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi Robert,&#010;&#010;&#010;On 10/6/14 11:31 AM, Robert Mark Bram wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A couple of questions about integration tests..&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1) Default vs non-default plugins&#010;&gt; I needed to include the maven-failsafe-plugin plugin to introduce&#010;&gt; integration tests into my project, but I didn't need to introduce the&#010;&gt; maven-surefire-plugin to my pom.xml for unit tests. Fair enough, but&#010;&gt; how do I know which plugins are included by default?&#010;&#010;This can be read here:&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/ref/3.1.1/maven-core/default-bindings.html&#010;&#010;There you can see for which packaging type which plugins are bound to &#010;the particular life cycle phases...&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) Just run integration tests?&#010;&gt; I can see that unit tests are all classes with names like *Test.java&#010;&gt; and integration tests are all classes with names like IT.java. But mvn&#010;&gt; verify and mvn test seem to run all tests (unit and integrations). Is&#010;&gt; there a way to run just one or the other?&#010;&#010;mvn test&#010;&#010;should not run integration tests...if it will so you have configured it &#010;wrong and not used maven-failsafe-plugin and bound to the wrong life &#010;cycle...cause the phases: pre-integration-test, integration-test and &#010;post-integration-test ran after package phase...&#010;So they will only be reached if you do&#010;&#010;mvn verify&#010;&#010;&#010;If you like to run only integration tests you can do this via &#010;configuring maven-surefire-plugin with a parameter skip...&#010;&#010;mvn -Dskip.unit.tests=true verify&#010;&#010;which will skip the unit tests but run the integration tests...&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3) Run integration tests after compile?&#010;&gt; The real reason for question 2 is that I wish to run integration tests&#010;&gt; only after I have deployed the new application to ensure the&#010;&gt; integration tests run on the server with the new content. Is there a&#010;&gt; way to do this?&#010;&#010;Based on the life cylce this is guaranteed...&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks for any assistance!&#010;&#010;You're welcome...&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Surefire plugin report all successfull sub tests.  
Date  :-

Hi Colleagues,&#010;&#010;Is there a possibility the surefire-plugin to count all successful subtest(verify statements)&#010;for Junit tests.&#010;&#010;Here is the describing of the problem:&#010;&gt; Imagine you have two tests, with each having 5 verify statements&#010;&gt; If both tests succeed, the test result will show two tests which passed successfully&#010;&gt; If only one test succeeds and the other test fails completely, the result (e.g. in Jenkins)&#010;will show one test succeeded and 5 tests failed, which leads to a success rate of ~17%, while&#010;in fact the success rate is 50% (5 verify statements of the succeeded test are only reported&#010;as one success).&#010;&#010;Thanks and regards,&#010;Mihail Chalashkanov&#010;&#010;&#010;

Best practice for integration tests (vs unit tests)

Right now I have an overlap of unit and integration tests and I want to&#010;tear out my integration tests and keep them separate. Name  :- 
Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarba...@gmx.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Best practice for integration tests (vs unit tests)  
Date  :-
Tue, 07 Oct 2014 23:44:02 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi Kevin,&#010;&#010;&#010;the best suggestion i can give is simply make a separate module where &#010;the integration tests should be moved to...&#010;&#010;&#010;This has the advantage having different location for them, cause they &#010;are more than unit tests which is expressed by using a separate module &#010;furthermore you have the configuration for the integration test within a &#010;separate module which is more flexible this includes the configuration &#010;of maven-failsafe-plugin as well.&#010;&#010;maven-failsafe-plugin should be used cause it supports a different &#010;naming schema for your integration tests (*IT.java see docs of &#010;maven-failsafe-plugin) and you can check the results of the integration &#010;tests via maven-failsafe-plugin:verify separately...and break the build &#010;if you like...&#010;&#010;Apart from the above integration tests should run at an other phase &#010;(pre-integration-test,integration-test, post-integration) and NOT in &#010;test phase...which is handled by maven-failsafe-plugin (see docs &#010;http://maven.apache.org/surefire/maven-failsafe-plugin/usage.html)&#010;&#010;So if you like to run your unit tests parallel you can configure the &#010;maven-surefire-plugin which does not influence your integration tests...&#010;&#010;&#010;I would also suggest to put the integration tests into src/test/java &#010;within the separated module....&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;On 10/8/14 1:28 AM, Kevin Burton wrote:&#010;&gt; Right now I have an overlap of unit and integration tests and I want to&#010;&gt; tear out my integration tests and keep them separate.  This way our unit&#010;&gt; tests execute fast and integration testing takes a bit longer.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; … and now I’m trying to figure out the best strategy for that.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Reading this:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://docs.codehaus.org/display/MAVENUSER/Maven+and+Integration+Testing&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; seems to not solve the problem.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Seems to me the easiest would be to just have src/main/integration-tests&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; … but would I have to use failsafe or surefire?  I’m not sure why I would&#010;&gt; need another plugin for this.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Maybe someone can enlightenment me with some maven wisdom?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
Rather than having two different server sections in settings.xml it is better to use one and&#010;the same id in the distribtutionMgt in the pom if they are for the same server. So e.g. if&#010;you deploy everything to nexus it could look like this&#010;&#010;&lt;distributionManagement&gt;&#010;   &lt;repository&gt;&#010;      &lt;id&gt;nexus&lt;/id&gt;&#010;      &lt;url&gt;http://localhost:8081/nexus/content/repositories/releases&lt;/url&gt;&#010;    &lt;/repository&gt;&#010;    &lt;snapshotRepository&gt;&#010;      &lt;id&gt;nexus&lt;/id&gt;&#010;      &lt;url&gt;http://localhost:8081/nexus/content/repositories/snapshots&lt;/url&gt;&#010;    &lt;/snapshotRepository&gt;&#010;    &lt;site&gt;&#010;      &lt;id&gt;nexus&lt;/id&gt;&#010;      &lt;url&gt;dav:http://localhost:8081/nexus/content/sites/site-internal/example&lt;/url&gt;&#010;    &lt;/site&gt;&#010;  &lt;/distributionManagement&gt;&#010;&#010;and then settings just needs &#010;&#010;&lt;server&gt;&#010;&lt;id&gt;nexus&lt;/id&gt;&#010;....&#010;&#010;The same id is also used if you set up mirror in settings e.g.&#010;&#010;  &lt;mirror&gt;&#010;&lt;id&gt;nexus&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&#010;causes the same credentials to be used for accessing the mirror url. You can use that to e.g.&#010;disable anonymous access on Nexus and then require credentials.&#010;&#010;manfred&#010;&#010;DJViking wrote on 08.10.2014 03:06:&#010;&#010;&gt; That was it. &#010;&gt;        &lt;snapshotRepository&gt;&#010;&gt;            &lt;id&gt;snapshots&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;           &#010;&gt; &lt;url&gt;http://maven-vm1:8081/nexus/content/repositories/snapshots&lt;/url&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;/snapshotRepository&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;repository&gt;&#010;&gt;            &lt;id&gt;releases&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;           &#010;&gt; &lt;url&gt;http://maven-vm1:8081/nexus/content/repositories/releases&lt;/url&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;/repository&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I had to create two servers with both these Id's, then it worked just fine.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Maybe I missed it, but I couldn't find anywhere in the documentation that&#010;&gt; this id needed to match the id in the server.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/maven-deploy-artifacts-to-Nexus-repository-tp5751512p5808061.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Kristian Rosenvold &lt;kristian.rosenv...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Why do running modules in parallel take longer to execute than running them in sequence?  
Date  :-
Thu, 09 Oct 2014 06:28:18 GMT  
contents:- 
You are right that the -T option and surefire's parallelism are&#010;complementary. Given equal-sized modules the effect tweaking surefire&#010;vs -T parallelism should be similar.&#010;&#010;The fork/thread related parameters to surefire have NO relation to the&#010;-T parameters, which means "reuseForks" is ineffective in your&#010;settings.&#010;&#010;I suspect you're simply trashing your os or the VM. Look at&#010;disk/memory usage indicators OS level. In terms of resource efficiency&#010;there's a clear difference between the different alternatives:&#010;&#010;A) Multiple threads within same (or a single forked) VM inside&#010;surefire. By far the most resource efficient (Probably 10x faster than&#010;the alternatives)&#010;B) Multiple surefire forks (Can be resource heavy too !)&#010;C) -T n option, which can  amplify other settings "n-fold".&#010;&#010;Kristian&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-10-08 21:11 GMT+02:00 laredotornado-3 &lt;laredotornado@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Karl, to answer your question, I only have one processor on my MacBook Pro&#010;&gt; (10.9.5), which is a 2.2 GHz Intel Core i7.  I haven't set "forkCount" in&#010;&gt; either my surefire or failsafe plugin (configs listed in question) because I&#010;&gt; was under the impression that the "-T" option took care of that.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jörg, My $MAVEN_OPTS var is set to -Xmx4096m, but I thought I read somewhere&#010;&gt; that in the case of surefire/failsafe, MAVEN_OPTS is ignored in favor of the&#010;&gt; configurations listed in the plugins, which are "-Xmx2048m&#010;&gt; -XX:MaxPermSize=512M" for surefire and "-Xmx4096m -XX:MaxPermSize=512M" for&#010;&gt; failsafe.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks, - Dave&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Why-do-running-modules-in-parallel-take-longer-to-execute-than-running-them-in-sequence-tp5808128p5808146.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Thu, 09 Oct 2014 02:53:20 GMT

I have a client and server in a multi-module.&#010;&#010;How do I test them ? Name  :- 
Barrie Treloar &lt;baerr...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How do I test client and server since they form circular dependencies?  
Date  :-
Thu, 09 Oct 2014 04:19:40 GMT  
contents:- 
On 9 October 2014 13:49, Bernd Eckenfels &lt;ecki@zusammenkunft.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Am Wed, 8 Oct 2014 19:53:20 -0700&#010;&gt; schrieb Kevin Burton &lt;burton@spinn3r.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; maybe one idea is to build a meta-module like foo-client-server-test&#010;&gt; &gt; which as a dependency on foo-client and foo-server.  then they could&#010;&gt; &gt; each test each other?  Seems a bit of a hack but it should work ..&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Yes, have an integration test module in your reactor which depends on&#010;&gt; both. Thats not a hack, is a good way to do that.&#010;&#010;&#010;A circular dependency is normally a sign that you haven't got your&#010;separations right.&#010;&#010;In order to run your test you need to use both the server and client, that&#010;sounds like a dependency to me!&#010;And so you need a new module to express that dependency in.&#010;&#010;

Well the question you really will want to know is:&#010;&#010;"do I want any other modules to depend on the integration tests being&#010;successful?"&#010;&#010;If the answer is "yes" then you will most likely need to deploy something&#010;(&lt;packaging&gt;pom&lt;/packaging&gt;) and that may require adding the missing&#010;bindings into the lifecycle.&#010;&#010;If the answer is "no" then you will just configure the integration test&#010;module with&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&lt;artifactId&gt;maven-deploy-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&lt;/configuration&gt;&lt;skip&gt;true&lt;/skip&gt;&lt;/configuration&gt;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;On 9 October 2014 09:23, Robert Mark Bram &lt;&#010;robertmarkbram+mailing.lists@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; My parent POM declares this Selenium project in a profile.&#010;&gt;    &lt;profile&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;id&gt;default-build&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;!-- This profile will be active if another profile isn't triggered&#010;&gt;       &lt;/modules&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;/profile&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; And the Selenium pom (sub-module) has the following:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Packaging&#010;&gt;    &lt;packaging&gt;jar&lt;/packaging&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Re: What packaging to use for a sub-module that just runs integration tests?

&gt; Well the question you really will want to know is:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; "do I want any other modules to depend on the integration tests being&#010;&gt; successful?"&#010;&#010;The Hatter opened his eyes very wide on hearing this; but all he said&#010;was, "Why is a mvn like a writing-desk?"&#010;&#010;&gt; If the answer is "no" then you will just configure the integration test&#010;&gt; module with&#010;&gt; &lt;plugin&gt;&lt;artifactId&gt;maven-deploy-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&lt;/configuration&gt;&lt;skip&gt;true&lt;/skip&gt;&lt;/configuration&gt;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Thanks again Stephen - nail, head and hammer. Name  :- 
Tony Jewell &lt;tony.jew...@cregganna.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Request for functionality in maven-assembly-plugin - ignoreProjectBuildFilters  
Date  :-
Sun, 12 Oct 2014 23:09:52 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;We hit an issue when using maven-assembly-plugin:2.4.1.&#010;&#010;We were using filters in assemblies to filter config property files&#010;according to the assembly we were producing - thus targetting our various&#010;environments.&#010;&#010;In the Project Build we defined test filter sources for tests and running&#010;in the IDE.&#010;&#010;Unfortunately, the default action in maven-assembly-plugin is to include&#010;all ${project.build.filters} - before the filters defined in the Assembly&#010;configuration. This meant all our assemblies had the Test configs.&#010;&#010;I have attached an example project that displays the issue and a patch to&#010;the current trunk maven-assembly-plugin:2.4.2-SNAPSHOT.&#010;&#010;A snippet from sample pom.xml showing the proposed new&#010;ignoreProjectBuildFilters config boolean usage is:&#010;&#010;          &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;              &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;              &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-assembly-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;              &lt;version&gt;${maven-assembly-plugin.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;              &lt;executions&gt;&#010;                  &lt;execution&gt;&#010;                      &lt;id&gt;prod-assemble&lt;/id&gt;&#010;                      &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;                      &lt;goals&gt;&lt;goal&gt;single&lt;/goal&gt;&lt;/goals&gt;&#010;                      &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                          &lt;!-- Do not include the Filters as defined in the&#010;Project Build --&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;includeProjectBuildFilters&gt;false&lt;/includeProjectBuildFilters&gt;&#010;                          &lt;filters&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;filter&gt;src/main/filters/prod.properties&lt;/filter&gt;&#010;                          &lt;/filters&gt;&#010;                          &lt;descriptors&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;descriptors&gt;src/main/assemblies/prod-assemble.xml&lt;/descriptors&gt;&#010;                          &lt;/descriptors&gt;&#010;                      &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;                  &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;              &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;          &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Tony Jewell&#010;Cregganna Computer Consultants Ltd&#010;&#010;  

================

Name  :- 
Thomas Broyer &lt;t.bro...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
How to resolve artifacts while respecting projects' dependency management? (or finding an alternative)  
Date  :-
Sun, 12 Oct 2014 23:17:58 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi all,&#010;&#010;I have a situation where a plugin needs to take the project's classpath and&#010;add some elements to it. What I'd like is that the elements be resolved as&#010;if they were declared as dependencies in the project's POM: take into&#010;account dependencyManagement for the artifact's version and (more&#010;importantly) its transitive dependencies.&#010;How to do it? (in a way compatible with all Maven 3.x releases)&#010;&#010;Or do you think it'd be a better approach to just ask people add those&#010;dependencies to their projects? They're tools needed for building the&#010;project, but they don't need to be in the javac classpath. I tend to&#010;believe this approach is much cleaner, but would appreciate external&#010;feedback.&#010;The plugin currently resolves the dependencies using maven-compat's&#010;ArtifactResolver but I don't think this respects the projects&#010;dependencyManagement (BTW, the "root" artifact passed comes from the&#010;pluginArtifactMap); it also unconditionally add the JARs to the classpath,&#010;which could cause conflicts I believe in some (edge-case) conditions. The&#010;first question I asked because I'd like to keep backwards compatibility and&#010;try to fix things (or at least make them better), but if the best practice&#010;is to add the dependencies to the project using the plugin, I'd just leave&#010;resolution as it is today but disable it behind a flag (either the plugin&#010;extends the classpath in some "broken" way, or you add the dependencies to&#010;your project and the plugin just uses the project's classpath).&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Thomas Broyer&#010;/tɔ.ma.bʁwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&#010;  

================

Name  :- 
Anders Hammar &lt;and...@hammar.net&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How to resolve artifacts while respecting projects' dependency management? (or finding an alternative)  
Date  :-
Mon, 13 Oct 2014 05:53:03 GMT  
contents:- 
If it is a dependency only needed by the plugin in question (during build&#010;time) it should not be added to the project's dependencies. However, it&#010;should probably be added as a dependency to the plugin in the pom, hich&#010;will add it to the classpath for the plugin execution. However, AFAIK that&#010;section does not honor versions declared in the depMgmt section.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;On Mon, Oct 13, 2014 at 1:17 AM, Thomas Broyer &lt;t.broyer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have a situation where a plugin needs to take the project's classpath and&#010;&gt; add some elements to it. What I'd like is that the elements be resolved as&#010;&gt; if they were declared as dependencies in the project's POM: take into&#010;&gt; account dependencyManagement for the artifact's version and (more&#010;&gt; importantly) its transitive dependencies.&#010;&gt; How to do it? (in a way compatible with all Maven 3.x releases)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Or do you think it'd be a better approach to just ask people add those&#010;&gt; dependencies to their projects? They're tools needed for building the&#010;&gt; project, but they don't need to be in the javac classpath. I tend to&#010;&gt; believe this approach is much cleaner, but would appreciate external&#010;&gt; feedback.&#010;&gt; The plugin currently resolves the dependencies using maven-compat's&#010;&gt; ArtifactResolver but I don't think this respects the projects&#010;&gt; dependencyManagement (BTW, the "root" artifact passed comes from the&#010;&gt; pluginArtifactMap); it also unconditionally add the JARs to the classpath,&#010;&gt; which could cause conflicts I believe in some (edge-case) conditions. The&#010;&gt; first question I asked because I'd like to keep backwards compatibility and&#010;&gt; try to fix things (or at least make them better), but if the best practice&#010;&gt; is to add the dependencies to the project using the plugin, I'd just leave&#010;&gt; resolution as it is today but disable it behind a flag (either the plugin&#010;&gt; extends the classpath in some "broken" way, or you add the dependencies to&#010;&gt; your project and the plugin just uses the project's classpath).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Thomas Broyer&#010;&gt; /tɔ.ma.bʁwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt; &lt;&#010;&gt; http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;  

================

Name  :- 
Thomas Broyer &lt;t.bro...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How to resolve artifacts while respecting projects' dependency management? (or finding an alternative)  
Date  :-
Mon, 13 Oct 2014 09:13:34 GMT  
contents:- 
On Mon, Oct 13, 2014 at 7:53 AM, Anders Hammar &lt;anders@hammar.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; If it is a dependency only needed by the plugin in question (during build&#010;&gt; time) it should not be added to the project's dependencies. However, it&#010;&gt; should probably be added as a dependency to the plugin in the pom, hich&#010;&gt; will add it to the classpath for the plugin execution. However, AFAIK that&#010;&gt; section does not honor versions declared in the depMgmt section.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Remember, the goal is to add it to the project's deps to form a classpath&#010;(for a forked JVM or URLClassLoader).&#010;Not respecting dependencyManagement could cause conflicts and all sorts of&#010;weird, hard-to-diagnose, bugs.&#010;&#010;Actually, my use case is not much different from annotation processors&#010;(assuming you don't leverage -processorpath): annotation processors are&#010;only needed by the plugin running javac, but an annotation processor might&#010;have a transitive dependency that the project also uses (at a minimum the&#010;one that contains annotations that will be processed, but also various&#010;helpers to generate Java code; think auto-commons, javawriter, maybe even&#010;freemarker or velocity). What you'd want is the classpath containing the&#010;project dependencies, and the annotation processor and its dependencies&#010;that are not also project dependencies, all of that respecting&#010;dependencyManagement. Actually, you'd want the classpath to look exactly as&#010;if the annotation process was declared as a project dependency.&#010;&#010;The problem with "plugin dependencies" is that you have less control on the&#010;resolution process, specifically that dependencyManagement doesn't apply&#010;there (which is a good thing, as it could break the plugin!)&#010;Here, the plugin itself doesn't use the dependency so it doesn't need to be&#010;in the plugin's classloader; so using a plugin dependency does not seem to&#010;be a good idea either.&#010;&#010;Another example: imagine JUnit was split into 2 JARs: one with the APIs and&#010;one with the actual "runner". Now you'd include the former as a project&#010;dependency but would expect Surefire to provide the latter, but you'd want&#010;Surefire to use your project's dependencyManagement (let's say you use&#010;&lt;scope&gt;import&lt;/scope&gt; in your dependencyManagement to make sure all JUnit&#010;deps use the same version, for example). This is actually the exact use&#010;case I'm facing (just with other deps and another plugin); and in some&#010;cases the project will have a direct dependency on the "junit-runner", in&#010;which case you'd expect it to be used, and the plugin to not add anything.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; /Anders&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Mon, Oct 13, 2014 at 1:17 AM, Thomas Broyer &lt;t.broyer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I have a situation where a plugin needs to take the project's classpath&#010;&gt; and&#010;&gt; &gt; add some elements to it. What I'd like is that the elements be resolved&#010;&gt; as&#010;&gt; &gt; if they were declared as dependencies in the project's POM: take into&#010;&gt; &gt; account dependencyManagement for the artifact's version and (more&#010;&gt; &gt; importantly) its transitive dependencies.&#010;&gt; &gt; How to do it? (in a way compatible with all Maven 3.x releases)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Or do you think it'd be a better approach to just ask people add those&#010;&gt; &gt; dependencies to their projects? They're tools needed for building the&#010;&gt; &gt; project, but they don't need to be in the javac classpath. I tend to&#010;&gt; &gt; believe this approach is much cleaner, but would appreciate external&#010;&gt; &gt; feedback.&#010;&gt; &gt; The plugin currently resolves the dependencies using maven-compat's&#010;&gt; &gt; ArtifactResolver but I don't think this respects the projects&#010;&gt; &gt; dependencyManagement (BTW, the "root" artifact passed comes from the&#010;&gt; &gt; pluginArtifactMap); it also unconditionally add the JARs to the&#010;&gt; classpath,&#010;&gt; &gt; which could cause conflicts I believe in some (edge-case) conditions. The&#010;&gt; &gt; first question I asked because I'd like to keep backwards compatibility&#010;&gt; and&#010;&gt; &gt; try to fix things (or at least make them better), but if the best&#010;&gt; practice&#010;&gt; &gt; is to add the dependencies to the project using the plugin, I'd just&#010;&gt; leave&#010;&gt; &gt; resolution as it is today but disable it behind a flag (either the plugin&#010;&gt; &gt; extends the classpath in some "broken" way, or you add the dependencies&#010;&gt; to&#010;&gt; &gt; your project and the plugin just uses the project's classpath).&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; --&#010;&gt; &gt; Thomas Broyer&#010;&gt; &gt; /tɔ.ma.bʁwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt; &lt;&#010;&gt; http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt; &lt;&#010;&gt; &gt; http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Thomas Broyer&#010;/tɔ.ma.bʁwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-

contents:- 
The Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Maven &#010;Compiler Plugin, version 3.2&#010;&#010;The Compiler Plugin is used to compile the sources of your project.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-compiler-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-compiler-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;3.2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Apache Maven Compiler Plugin - Version 3.2&#010;&#010;Task&#010;* [MCOMPILER-232] Fix RAT Report&#010;* [MCOMPILER-224] Maven compiler plugin does not properly consume plexus &#010;compiler output&#010;* [MCOMPILER-220] Fix o.a.m.p.c.CompilerMojoTestCase.testCompilerFork(), &#010;which fails when javac is not on the PATH&#010;* [MCOMPILER-159] generatedSourcesDirectory should be included in list &#010;provided by &#010;org.apache.maven.project.MavenProject.getCompileClasspathElements()&#010;* [MCOMPILER-157] Maven Compiler Plugin should add to compileSourceRoots &#010;for next plugins to consider as source directory for generated files&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;
